# 301\n
{Oxford, Bodleian Library, Junius 1, fols. 3r-: The Ormulum}\n
C12b2\n
510 320 N\n
{=Bourne, S Lincs=}\n
{=Sample tagged: fols. 3r-5ra; 9r-16vb. This comprises the\n
Dedication and Preface and Columns 1-44 of the Introduction\n
and Homilies, including all the material on the added leaves\n
up to this point. It is hoped that more will be added to this\n
sample later=}\n
{=Script - idiosyncratic, large, heavy, compressed script with strong\n
resemblances to Anglo-Saxon minuscule=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=For full bibliography and demonstration of a diplomatic transcription\n
including notice of 5 different colour-coded levels of correction by Orm\n
see  Nils-Lennart Johannesson, The Ormulum Project\n
http://www.english.su.se/nlj/ormproj/ormulum.htm. It will not be\n
practical here to notice the amount of detail given by Johannesson,\n
especially as access to the MS is now severely restricted. In the tagged\n
transcript below, made from photostats and microfilm, the usual\n
conventions apply. Doubled letters are realised as in the MS, either as e.g.\n
SS, when Orm writes the figurae side by side, or as e.g. R^R when he\n
stacks them on top of each other. y^y and w^w represent the doubled\n
vertically stacked thorn and wynn on a single ascender. Presence of an\n
accent is realised by following x, xx for double accents, xxx for\n
occasional triples; here these always follow the vowel, though in the\n
manuscript they often are placed over the following consonant, not on the\n
vowel itself. Microfilm and photostat do not show different coloured inks. No\n
attempt here is made to differentiate accents possibly added by others\n
than Orm except where Burchfield has noted their presence. A breve over a\n
vowel, indicating shortness is realised by lowercase v following the\n
vowel. Insular <g> is realised, as in my normal conventions, as g. His peculiar\n
flat-topped \'g\' that combines insular \'g\' and Caroline \'g\' is realised as\n
G, because in comparative studies it needs to be seen as equivalent to\n
other writers\' \'usual\' <g>-shapes. The third version of <g> to be\n
distinguished, ordinary Caroline <g>, used (usually doubled) for\n
/d3/, is here realised as G3. Orm is very consistent in his use of\n
majuscule or larger letter sizes for the beginning of every verse\n
line. Since he writes the verse continuously, and not in verse lines,\n
this is important and the capitalisation is retained as he has it.\n
He also, with great regularity, makes the Tironian sign where it\n
occurs at the beginning of a verse line much larger and bolder than\n
that which occurs mid-line - a sort of capital Tironian sign. I\n
have not marked these signs (realised according to my usual practice\n
as &) with an asterisk because I have not made such differentiations\n
to show size of Tironian symbol in other scribal texts. Punctuation\n
comprises punctus, punctus elevatus, positura (between sections)\n
and a dash, apparently used in the same way as in em or en dash in\n
PDE to indicate a pause or parenthesis. All punctuation is placed\n
in braces as usual. Punctus and punctus elevatus are realised in\n
the usual way with . and .\' . Positura is realised as ;. and dash\n
is realised as a hyphen. Orm has a hierarchal system of paragraphing\n
which he indicates by using paraphs of different size and pattern.\n
For this see Johannesson; I have not here differentiated between\n
different types of paraph. Holes and blemishes in the parchment,\n
which are numerous, are not noted here. Folio sizes and shapes\n
(and therefore line lengths) are very variable. No special notice\n
is given of this in the tagged text, although all line ends are\n
marked as usual. An early user of the MS, perhaps Junius or van\n
Vliet, has often added short downward strokes to separate words\n
that Orm had written very close together. These added strokes\n
are not noticed here. Where Orm himself has used separating\n
strokes - both above and below the minim height, these are\n
noted. Orm\'s formatting varies between single and double columns.\n
Where he uses double columns they are not ruled and in the\n
later-written prefatory material are very uneven in width. In such\n
cases they are usually divided by a long meandering hairline after\n
the writing of the first column and following its contours=}\n
{~f3r~}\n

$mo:digness/n<pr_MOD+Ig+NESSE $-ig/xs-aj-k_+Ig+ $-ness/xs-n<pr_+NESSE\n
{=Here Orm makes a broad upright stroke with a long \'headstroke\' like\n
a capital T about 2 cm to the left and 1.5 cm to the right. This\n
symbol reappears at the head of fol. 9r and it seems that Orm\n
intended the whole of what White-Holt label \'Preface\' to be\n
included here. I have not inserted that text here, however,\n
because it seems clearer with such a large block of text to\n
keep it in the place it is to be found in the MS and in the\n
only printed edition. The relevant text is on fols 9r-v where\n
it is cross-referenced to here=}\n
{para}\n

{\\}\n
{=From here until the end of fol. 8v (and continued on the second\n
half of fol. 9v) is taken up by a list of the titles and biblical\n
texts for Orm\'s projected contents. He lists 242 sermons of which\n
survive only 31 and some fragments. The table of contents is\n
entirely in Latin and I do not transcribe it here: see White and\n
Holt (1878: Texts). There follows on fol. 9r and the first half\n
of 9v the so-called Preface, which, judging from the matching\n
T-shaped sigla in the two relevant places in the text, Orm\n
intended to be inserted into the material on fol. 3v see above=}\n
{~f9r~}\n
{>)*ORMVLVM . \\ ORM .)>}\n
{=ins, in left hand margin in small neat capitals by a later hand=}\n
{=At the head of the single column of text appears a large T-shaped\n
siglum descending for five lines in the left margin and the cross-bar\n
of which is in the narrow top margin. This refers to the similar,\n
smaller version within the text on fol. 3v and implies that the\n
following text, until halfway down fol. 9va, should be inserted\n
into the text on fol. 3v=}\n
{para}\n

{=The rest of the folio contains the end of the contents and is\n

{~f10ra~}\n
{=Column 1=}\n
{=This is the true beginning of the Ormulum, having clearly been\n
written earlier than the prefatory materials and introduction.\n
The text is in two narrow columns, quite neat and straight in\n
the early folios, though there are later additions on small\n
scraps of parchment bound in at the correct places in the text.\n
The script is also smaller and neater than that employed by Orm\n
for the later-written prefatory materials=}\n
